                  </form>, (L,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">خُرُوجٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">مَخْرَجٌ</foreign>, (S, Msb, K,) <hi rend="ital">He,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it, went, came, passed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">got, out,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">forth; issued, emanated, proceeded, went,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">departed; contr. of</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">دَخَلَ</foreign>; (TA;) <foreign lang="ar">مِنَ المَوْضِعِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">from the place</hi>]. (Msb.) One says, <foreign lang="ar">خَرَجَ مَخْرَجًا حَسَنًا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it, went, came, passed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">got, out,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">forth,</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">well:</hi> and <hi rend="ital">it turned out well</hi>]. (S.) [And <foreign lang="ar">خَرَجَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">مِنْ طَاعَتِهِ</foreign>: see <foreign lang="ar">طَائِعٌ</foreign>, in art. <foreign lang="ar">طوع</foreign>. When <foreign lang="ar">خَرَجَ</foreign> means <hi rend="ital">It was disbursed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">expended,</hi> the inf. n. is <foreign lang="ar">خَرْجٌ</foreign>.] <foreign lang="ar">خَرَجَ بِهِ</foreign> [lit. <hi rend="ital">He went out,</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">with him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it</hi>]: see 4. (TA.) <foreign lang="ar">يَوْمُ الخُرُوجِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">The day of going forth</hi>] means <hi rend="ital">the day of the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عِيد</foreign> [or <hi rend="ital">festival</hi>]. (A, TA, from a trad.) And [as used in the Kur l. 41] <hi rend="ital">The day when men shall come forth from their graves;</hi> (TA;) a name of <hi rend="ital">the day of resurrection.</hi> (AO, K.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  [<assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">It became excluded</hi> by a definition or a rule or the like, or by a portion thereof.] <foreign lang="ar">مَنْصُوبٌ عَلَى الخُرُوجِ</foreign> is a phrase of the Basree grammarians, said of the objective complement of a verb, meaning <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">Put in the accus. case as being out of the predicament of the subject and that of the attribute.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">خَرَجَ مِنْ أَمْرٍ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  [<hi rend="ital">He got out of, escaped from, extricated himself from, evaded,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became quit of, affair,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">a state</hi>]. (ISh, TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">نكس</foreign>.) [And <foreign lang="ar">خَرَجَمِنْ حَالٍ إِلَى حَالٍ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical> <hi rend="ital">He passed from</hi> one <hi rend="ital">state to</hi> another <hi rend="ital">state.</hi> And <foreign lang="ar">خَرَجَ مِنْ دِينِهِ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical> <hi rend="ital">He quitted,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">forsook, his religion.</hi> And <foreign lang="ar">خَرَجَ</foreign>

                  <foreign lang="ar">دَيْنِهِ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical> <hi rend="ital">He paid such a one his debt:</hi> a phrase used in law. (TA.) [And <foreign lang="ar">خَرَجَ عَلَى السُّلْطَانِ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">عَنْ أَمْرِ السُّلْطَانِ</foreign>, <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">He rebelled against the Sultán.</hi>] And <foreign lang="ar">خَرَجَتْ عَلَى خِلْقَةِ الجَمَلِ</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  [<hi rend="ital">She became formed like the he-camel</hi>]; said of a she-camel that is termed   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n10271-1" target="مُخْتَرَجَةٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>. (S, A, K.) (L and K in art. <foreign lang="ar">خنذ</foreign>.) And <foreign lang="ar">خَرَجَ فِى العِلْمِ وَالصِّنَاعَةِ</foreign>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">خُرُوجٌ</foreign>, <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">He was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, conspicuous in science and art.</hi> (A, TA.                   <foreign lang="ar">السَّحَابُ</foreign>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">خُرُوجٌ</foreign>, meaning <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">The clouds became extended,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">expanded:</hi> see <foreign lang="ar">خَرْجٌ</foreign>.] And <foreign lang="ar">خَرَجَتِ السَّمَآءُ</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">The sky became clear, after having been cloudy.</hi> (T, A.)    </entryFree>26:Te8f,<entryFree id="n10272" key="خرّج" type="main">

                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">خرّج</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">خرج</orth>
                  </form>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">تَخْرِيجٌ</foreign>, [sometimes resembles in signification <foreign lang="ar">أَخْرَجَ</foreign>:] see the inf. n. voce <foreign lang="ar">خَرِيجٌ</foreign>.          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  [<assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">He resolved, explained,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">rendered,</hi> a saying. <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى هٰذَا خَرَّجُوا قَوْلَ كَذَا</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical> <hi rend="ital">According to this</hi> meaning &amp;c. <hi rend="ital">they have resolved, explained,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">rendered, such a saying,</hi> is a phrase of frequent occurrence in the larger lexicons &amp;c.]          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">He educated, disciplined,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">trained, well</hi> a youth: and in like manner, a horse [and a camel; for <foreign lang="ar">مُخَرَّجٌ</foreign>, as is indicated in the K voce <foreign lang="ar">مُدَرَّبٌ</foreign>, applied to a camel, is syn. with <foreign lang="ar">مُؤَدَّبٌ</foreign>]. (IAar.) You say, <foreign lang="ar">خرّجهُ فِى الأَدَبِ</foreign>, (S, A, * K,) inf. n. as above, <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">He educated, disciplined,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">trained, him well in polite accomplishments;</hi> i. e. a teacher, his pupil. (TA.)       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  [<hi rend="ital">He,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it, rendered</hi> a thing <foreign lang="ar">أَخْرَج</foreign>, i. e. <hi rend="ital">of two colours, white and black:</hi> &amp;c.] You say, <foreign lang="ar">النُّجُومُ تُخَرِّجُ اللَّوْنَ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The stars render the colour</hi> [of a thing, such as an expanse of water,] <hi rend="ital">a mixture of black and white,</hi> by reason of its blackness and their whiteness. (TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">خرّج اللَّوْحَ</foreign>, (A, K,) inf. n. as above, (K,) <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">He</hi> (a boy, A) <hi rend="ital">wrote upon part of the tablet and left part of it without writing.</hi> (A, * K.) And <foreign lang="ar">خرّج</foreign>

(S, K.) <foreign lang="ar">الخَرَاجُ بِالضَّمَانِ</foreign>, a saying ascribed to Mohammad, (K, TA,) occurring in a trad. of 'Áïsheh, of disputed authority, but affirmed by several authors to be genuine, means, accord. to most of the lawyers, (TA,) <hi rend="ital">The revenue</hi> derived from the slave <hi rend="ital">is</hi> the property of the purchaser <hi rend="ital">because of the responsibility</hi> which he has borne for him: (A, * Mgh, * K, TA:) for one purchases a slave, and imposes upon him the task of producing a revenue for a time, and then may discover in him a fault which the seller had concealed; wherefore he has a right to return him and to receive back the price; but the revenue which he had required the slave to produce is his lawful property, because he had been responsible for him; and if he had perished, part of his property had perished: (K, * TA:) in a similar manner IAth explains it, as relating to a male or female slave or to other property. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>
